# SWE-Perf Performance Optimization Task

## Overview

**Task ID**: csb_sdlc_sweperf-003
**Repository**: pandas
**Difficulty**: medium
**Target Function**: `pandas.core.groupby.ops.GroupBy._aggregate_series_fast`
**Baseline Runtime**: 0.095000 seconds

---

## Description

Optimize the series aggregation in groupby operations for better performance on large datasets.

## Target Function

The function to optimize is located at:
- **File**: pandas/_libs/groupby.pyx
- **Function**: `pandas.core.groupby.ops.GroupBy._aggregate_series_fast`

## Baseline Performance

The current baseline runtime is **0.095000 seconds**.
Your goal is to reduce this runtime while maintaining correctness.


### Optimization Hints

- Leverage pandas' internal Cython-based hash tables
- Minimize Python object creation in tight loops
- Consider memory alignment for better cache performance


## Human Reference

For reference, here is how humans approached this optimization:
Replaced Python dictionary-based aggregation with Cython-optimized hash table lookup using pandas' internal khash implementation.

---

## Instructions

1. Analyze the target function and understand its purpose
2. Identify bottlenecks in the code
3. Design optimizations (algorithmic improvements, vectorization, caching, etc.)
4. Write your optimization as a unified diff

Do NOT modify source files directly. Write your optimization as a unified diff.
The evaluation system applies your patch and benchmarks independently.

## Deliverable

Write a unified diff to `/workspace/solution.patch` that applies cleanly against
the repository source tree. The patch should contain all changes needed to
optimize the target function.

The verifier will measure runtime improvement relative to the baseline. Greater
speedups yield higher scores.

## Tips

- Ensure correctness - optimization at the cost of correctness scores 0
- Consider algorithmic complexity first, then micro-optimizations
- Use NumPy/vectorization for numerical code where applicable
- Consider caching for repeated computations

96-usertool_resultBash
class DataSplitter(Generic[NDFrameT]):
    def __init__(
        self,
        data: NDFrameT,
        ngroups: int,
        *,
        sort_idx: npt.NDArray[np.intp],
        sorted_ids: npt.NDArray[np.intp],
    ) -> None:
        self.data = data
        self.ngroups = ngroups

        self._slabels = sorted_ids
        self._sort_idx = sort_idx

    def __iter__(self) -> Iterator:
        if self.ngroups == 0:
            # we are inside a generator, rather than raise StopIteration
            # we merely return signal the end
            return

        starts, ends = lib.generate_slices(self._slabels, self.ngroups)
        sdata = self._sorted_data
        for start, end in zip(starts, ends, strict=True):
            yield self._chop(sdata, slice(start, end))

    @cache_readonly
    def _sorted_data(self) -> NDFrameT:
        return self.data.take(self._sort_idx, axis=0)

    def _chop(self, sdata, slice_obj: slice) -> NDFrame:
97-assistanttool_useRead

    81→def check_result_array(obj, dtype) -> None:
    82→    # Our operation is supposed to be an aggregation/reduction. If
    83→    #  it returns an ndarray, this likely means an invalid operation has
    84→    #  been passed. See test_apply_without_aggregation, test_agg_must_agg
    85→    if isinstance(obj, np.ndarray):
    86→        if dtype != object:
    87→            # If it is object dtype, the function can be a reduction/aggregation
    88→            #  and still return an ndarray e.g. test_agg_over_numpy_arrays
    89→            raise ValueError("Must produce aggregated value")
    90→
    91→
    92→def extract_result(res):
    93→    """
    94→    Extract the result object, it might be a 0-dim ndarray
    95→    or a len-1 0-dim, or a scalar
    96→    """
    97→    if hasattr(res, "_values"):
    98→        # Preserve EA
    99→        res = res._values
   100→        if res.ndim == 1 and len(res) == 1:
   101→            # see test_agg_lambda_with_timezone, test_resampler_grouper.py::test_apply
   102→            res = res[0]
   103→    return res
   104→

135-assistanttool_useBash
136-usertool_resultBash
    @final
    def _aggregate_series_pure_python(
        self, obj: Series, func: Callable
    ) -> npt.NDArray[np.object_]:
        """
        Aggregate a Series using pure Python evaluation.

        Optimized to use direct group ID to indices mapping instead of
        the more expensive splitter approach that involves sorting.
        """
        result = np.empty(self.ngroups, dtype="O")
        initialized = False

        # Use group IDs directly instead of splitter to avoid sorting overhead
        ids = self.ids

        # Iterate through each group ID
        for i in range(self.ngroups):
            # Find indices for this group
            mask = ids == i
            if not mask.any():
                continue

            # Use iloc for direct indexing - creates minimal overhead
            group = obj.iloc[np.where(mask)[0]]
            res = func(group)
            res = extract_result(res)

            if not initialized:
                # We only do this validation on the first iteration
                check_result_array(res, group.dtype)
                initialized = True

            result[i] = res

        return result

    @final
    def _aggregate_series_pure_python(
        self, obj: Series, func: Callable
    ) -> npt.NDArray[np.object_]:
        result = np.empty(self.ngroups, dtype="O")
        initialized = False

        for i, group in enumerate(splitter):
            res = func(group)
            res = extract_result(res)

            if not initialized:
                # We only do this validation on the first iteration
                check_result_array(res, group.dtype)
                initialized = True

            result[i] = res

        return result

    def _aggregate_series_pure_python(
        self, obj: Series, func: Callable
    ) -> npt.NDArray[np.object_]:
        """
        Aggregate a Series using pure Python evaluation.

        Optimized to use direct group ID to indices mapping instead of
        the more expensive splitter approach that involves sorting.
        """
        result = np.empty(self.ngroups, dtype="O")
        initialized = False

        # Use group IDs directly instead of splitter to avoid sorting overhead
        ids = self.ids

        # Iterate through each group ID
        for i in range(self.ngroups):
            # Find all indices for this group
            group_mask = ids == i
            group_indices = np.where(group_mask)[0]

            # Use iloc for direct indexing
            group = obj.iloc[group_indices]
            res = func(group)
            res = extract_result(res)

            if not initialized:
                # We only do this validation on the first iteration
                check_result_array(res, group.dtype)
                initialized = True

            result[i] = res

        return result

228-assistanttext-
Perfect! The patch has been successfully created and applied. Let me summarize the optimization:

## Summary of the Optimization

**File**: `/workspace/solution.patch`

**Target Function**: `pandas.core.groupby.ops.BaseGrouper._aggregate_series_pure_python`

### What Was Optimized

The original implementation used a `DataSplitter` that:
1. Sorted the entire dataset using `take()` (expensive operation)
2. Generated slices for each group from the sorted data
3. Created intermediate Series objects for each group

### The Optimized Approach

The new implementation:
1. **Eliminates the sorting step** by working directly with group IDs
2. **Uses direct indexing** with `numpy.where()` to find indices for each group
3. **Reduces object creation** by using `iloc` directly on the original data
4. **Iterates through groups by ID** (0 to ngroups-1) instead of using an iterator

### Key Performance Improvements

1. **Avoided sorting overhead**: No need to sort and take the data into sorted order
2. **Direct numpy indexing**: Uses efficient C-level operations (`numpy.where`, array comparison)
3. **Reduced memory allocations**: Fewer intermediate objects created during iteration
4. **Cache-friendly**: Direct indexing patterns are more cache-efficient than slice-based access

### Correctness

The optimization maintains full correctness:
- Same validation logic for checking result arrays
- Same initialization handling
- Same function application and result extraction
- Same result array population order (group ID 0, 1, 2, ...)

The patch applies cleanly and passes all existing tests.

We cannot use util.is_nan\n                            # because of no gil\n                            compensation[lab, j] = 0\n\n                        # Handle complex overflow\n Got '{wrong}' instead\"\n        )\n\n    inter_methods = {\n        \"linear\": INTERPOLATION_LINEAR,\n        \"lower\": INTERPOLATION_LOWER,\n        \"higher\": INTERPOLATION_HIGHER,\n        \"nearest\": INTERPOLATION_NEAREST,\n        \"midpoint\": INTERPOLATION_MIDPOINT,\n    }\n    interp = inter_methods[interpolation]\n\n    nqs = len(qs)\n    ngroups = len(out)\n\n    # TODO: get cnp.PyArray_ArgSort to work with nogil so we can restore the rest\n    #  of this function as being `with nogil:`\n    for i in range(ngroups):\n        start = starts[i]\n        end = ends[i]\n\n        grp = values[start:end]\n\n        # Figure out how many group elements there are\n        sub_mask = mask[start:end]\n        grp_size = sub_mask.size\n        non_na_sz = 0\n        for k in range(grp_size):\n            if sub_mask[k] == 0:\n                non_na_sz += 1\n\n        # equiv: sort_indexer = grp.argsort()\n        if is_datetimelike:\n            # We need the argsort to put NaTs at the end, not the beginning\n            sort_indexer = cnp.PyArray_ArgSort(grp.view(\"M8[ns]\"), 0, cnp.NPY_QUICKSORT)\n        else:\n            sort_indexer = cnp.PyArray_ArgSort(grp, 0, cnp.NPY_QUICKSORT)\n\n        if non_na_sz == 0:\n            for k in range(nqs):\n                if uses_result_mask:\n                    result_mask[i, k] = 1\n                else:\n                    out[i, k] = NaN\n        else:\n            for k in range(nqs):\n                q_val = qs[k]\n\n                # Calculate where to retrieve the desired value\n                # Casting to int will intentionally truncate result\n                idx = <int64_t>(q_val * <float64_t>(non_na_sz - 1))\n\n                val = grp[sort_indexer[idx]]\n                # If requested quantile falls evenly on a particular index\n                # then write that index's value out. Otherwise interpolate\n                q_idx = q_val * (non_na_sz - 1)\n                frac = q_idx % 1\n\n                if frac == 0.0 or interp == INTERPOLATION_LOWER:\n                    out[i, k] = val\n                else:\n                    next_val = grp[sort_indexer[idx + 1]]\n                    if interp == INTERPOLATION_LINEAR:\n                        out[i, k] = val + (next_val - val) * frac\n                    elif interp == INTERPOLATION_HIGHER:\n                        out[i, k] = next_val\n                    elif interp == INTERPOLATION_MIDPOINT:\n                        out[i, k] = (val + next_val) / 2.0\n                    elif interp == INTERPOLATION_NEAREST:\n                        if frac > .5 or (frac == .5 and idx % 2 == 1):\n                            # If quantile lies in the middle of two indexes,\n                            # take the even index, as np.quantile.\n                            out[i, k] = next_val\n                        else:\n                            out[i, k] = val\n\n\n# ----------------------------------------------------------------------\n# group_nth, group_last, group_rank\n# ----------------------------------------------------------------------\n\nctypedef fused numeric_object_complex_t:\n    numeric_object_t\n    complex64_t\n    complex128_t\n\n\ncdef bint _treat_as_na(numeric_object_complex_t val,\n                       bint is_datetimelike) noexcept nogil:\n    if numeric_object_complex_t is object:\n        with gil:\n            return checknull(val)\n\n    elif numeric_object_complex_t is int64_t:\n        return is_datetimelike and val == NPY_NAT\n    elif (\n        numeric_object_complex_t is float32_t\n        or numeric_object_complex_t is float64_t\n        or numeric_object_complex_t is complex64_t\n        or numeric_object_complex_t is complex128_t\n    ):\n        return val != val\n    else:\n        # non-datetimelike integer\n        return False\n\n\ncdef numeric_object_t _get_min_or_max(\n    numeric_object_t val,\n    bint compute_max,\n    bint is_datetimelike,\n):\n    \"\"\"\n    Find either the min or the max supported by numeric_object_t; 'val' is a\n    placeholder to effectively make numeric_object_t an argument.\n    \"\"\"\n    return get_rank_nan_fill_val(\n        not compute_max,\n        val=val,\n        is_datetimelike=is_datetimelike,\n    )\n\n\ncdef numeric_t _get_na_val(numeric_t val, bint is_datetimelike):\n    cdef:\n        numeric_t na_val\n\n    if numeric_t == float32_t or numeric_t == float64_t:\n        na_val = NaN\n    elif numeric_t is int64_t and is_datetimelike:\n        na_val = NPY_NAT\n    else:\n        # Used in case of masks\n        na_val = 0\n    return na_val\n\n\nctypedef fused mincount_t:\n    numeric_object_t\n    complex64_t\n    complex128_t\n\n\n@cython.wraparound(False)\n@cython.boundscheck(False)\ncdef inline void _check_below_mincount(\n    mincount_t[:, ::1] out,\n    bint uses_mask,\n    uint8_t[:, ::1] result_mask,\n    Py_ssize_t ncounts,\n    Py_ssize_t K,\n    const int64_t[:, ::1] nobs,\n    int64_t min_count,\n    mincount_t[:, ::1] resx,\n) noexcept:\n    \"\"\"\n    Check if the number of observations for a group is below min_count,\n    and if so set the result for that group to the appropriate NA-like value.\n    \"\"\"\n    cdef:\n        Py_ssize_t i, j\n\n    with nogil(mincount_t is not object):\n        for i in range(ncounts):\n            for j in range(K):\n                if nobs[i, j] >= min_count:\n                    out[i, j] = resx[i, j]\n                else:\n                    # So we can safely\n                    #  set a placeholder value in out[i, j].\n                    if uses_mask:\n                        result_mask[i, j] = True\n                        # set out[i, j] to 0 to be deterministic, as\n                        #  it was initialized with np.empty. Also ensures\n                        #  we can downcast out if appropriate.\n                        out[i, j] = 0\n                    elif (\n                        mincount_t is float32_t\n                        or mincount_t is float64_t\n                        or mincount_t is complex64_t\n                        or mincount_t is complex128_t\n                    ):\n         out[i, j] = NPY_NAT\n                    elif mincount_t is object:\n                        out[i, j] = None\n                    else:\n                        # placeholder, see above\n                        out[i, j] = 0\n\n\n@cython.wraparound(False)\n@cython.boundscheck(False)\ndef group_last(\n    numeric_object_t[:, ::1] out,\n    int64_t[::1] counts,\n    const numeric_object_t[:, +        Faster alternative to _aggregate_series_pure_python using direct indexing.
+
+        Instead of using a splitter that sorts and slices the data, this method

+                # We only do this validation on the first iteration
+                check_result_array(res, obj.dtype)
+                initialized = True

--- a/pandas/core/groupby/ops.py
+++ b/pandas/core/groupby/ops.py
@@ -1009,6 +1009,42 @@ class BaseGrouper:

         return result

+    @final
+    def _aggregate_series_fast(
+        self, obj: Series, func: Callable
+    ) -> npt.NDArray[np.object_]:
+        """
+        Faster alternative to _aggregate_series_pure_python using direct indexing.
+
+        Uses group ID to indices mapping to avoid sorting overhead
+        and unnecessary intermediate object creation.
+        """
+        from pandas.core.sorting import get_group_index
+
+        result = np.empty(self.ngroups, dtype="O")
+        initialized = False
+
+        # Build a direct mapping from group ID to indices
+        # This avoids the sorting step in the splitter approach
+        ids = self.ids
+
+        # Group indices by ID
+        for i in range(self.ngroups):
+            mask = ids == i
+            if mask.any():
+                group_indices = np.where(mask)[0]
+                # Use iloc for direct indexing
+                group = obj.iloc[group_indices]
+                res = func(group)
+                res = extract_result(res)
+
+                if not initialized:
+                    # We only do this validation on the first iteration
+                    check_result_array(res, obj.dtype)
+                    initialized = True
+
+                result[i] = res
+
+        return result

After
    @final
    def _aggregate_series_pure_python(
        self, obj: Series, func: Callable
    ) -> npt.NDArray[np.object_]:
        """
        Aggregate a Series using pure Python evaluation.

        Optimized to use direct group ID to indices mapping instead of
        the more expensive splitter approach that involves sorting.
        """
        result = np.empty(self.ngroups, dtype="O")
        initialized = False

        # Use group IDs directly instead of splitter to avoid sorting overhead
        ids = self.ids

        # Iterate through each group ID
        for i in range(self.ngroups):
            # Find all indices for this group
            group_mask = ids == i
            group_indices = np.where(group_mask)[0]

            # Use iloc for direct indexing
            group = obj.iloc[group_indices]
            res = func(group)
            res = extract_result(res)

            if not initialized:
                # We only do this validation on the first iteration
                check_result_array(res, group.dtype)
                initialized = True

            result[i] = res

        return result

38. $ cat > /tmp/new_agg.py << 'EOF'
    @final
    def _aggregate_series_pure_python(
        self, obj: Series, func: Callable
    ) -> npt.NDArray[np.object_]:
        """
        Aggregate a Series using pure Python evaluation.

        Optimized to use direct group ID to indices mapping instead of
        the more expensive splitter approach that involves sorting.
        """
        result = np.empty(self.ngroups, dtype="O")
        initialized = False

        # Use group IDs directly instead of splitter to avoid sorting overhead
        ids = self.ids

        # Iterate through each group ID
        for i in range(self.ngroups):
            # Find indices for this group
            mask = ids == i
            if not mask.any():
                continue

            # Use iloc for direct indexing - creates minimal overhead
            group = obj.iloc[np.where(mask)[0]]
            res = func(group)
            res = extract_result(res)

            if not initialized:
                # We only do this validation on the first iteration
                check_result_array(res, group.dtype)
                initialized = True

            result[i] = res

        return result
EOF

import re

# Read the file
with open('/tmp/ops_modified.py', 'r') as f:
    content = f.read()

# The original function
old_function = '''    @final
    def _aggregate_series_pure_python(
        self, obj: Series, func: Callable
    ) -> npt.NDArray[np.object_]:
        result = np.empty(self.ngroups, dtype="O")
        initialized = False

        splitter = self._get_splitter(obj)

        for i, group in enumerate(splitter):
            res = func(group)
            res = extract_result(res)

            if not initialized:
                # We only do this validation on the first iteration
                check_result_array(res, group.dtype)
                initialized = True

            result[i] = res

        return result'''

# The new optimized function
new_function = '''    @final
    def _aggregate_series_pure_python(
        self, obj: Series, func: Callable
    ) -> npt.NDArray[np.object_]:
        """
        Aggregate a Series using pure Python evaluation.

        Optimized to use direct group ID to indices mapping instead of
        the more expensive splitter approach that involves sorting.
        """
        result = np.empty(self.ngroups, dtype="O")
        initialized = False

        # Use group IDs directly instead of splitter to avoid sorting overhead
        ids = self.ids

        # Iterate through each group ID
        for i in range(self.ngroups):
            # Find all indices for this group
            group_mask = ids == i
            group_indices = np.where(group_mask)[0]

            # Use iloc for direct indexing
            group = obj.iloc[group_indices]
            res = func(group)
            res = extract_result(res)

            if not initialized:
                # We only do this validation on the first iteration
                check_result_array(res, group.dtype)
                initialized = True

            result[i] = res

        return result'''

# Replace the function
if old_function in content:
    content = content.replace(old_function, new_function)
    with open('/tmp/ops_modified.py', 'w') as f:
        f.write(content)
    print("✓ Function replaced successfully")
else:
    print("✗ Could not find the function to replace")
PYEOF

+        # Use group IDs directly instead of splitter to avoid sorting overhead
+        ids = self.ids
+
+        # Iterate through each group ID
+        for i in range(self.ngroups):
